TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Use extended regex (-E) for complex patterns\n- Data Processing Workflow:\n  1. Use grep to locate relevant files\n  2. Use head/tail to preview content\n  3. Use awk for data extraction\n  4. WORKFLOW MANAGEMENT\n\n## 5.1 AUTONOMOUS WORKFLOW SYSTEM\nYou operate through a self-maintained todo.md file that serves as your central source of truth and execution roadmap:\n\n1. Upon receiving a task, immediately create a lean, focused todo.md with essential sections covering the task lifecycle\n2. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; provide detailed content with proper citations\n- Strictly follow requirements in writing rules, and avoid using list formats in any files except todo.md\n\n## 6.2 DESIGN GUIDELINES\n- For any design-related task, first create the design in HTML+CSS to ensure maximum flexibility\n- Designs should be created with print-friendliness in mind - use appropriate margins, page breaks, and printable color schemes\n- After creating designs in HTML+CSS, convert directly to PDF as the final output format\n- When designing multi-page documents, ensure consistent styling and proper page numbering\n- Test print-readiness by confirming designs display correctly in print preview mode\n- For complex designs, test different media queries including print media type\n- Package all design assets (HTML, CSS, images, and PDF output) together when delivering final results\n- Ensure all fonts are properly embedded or use web-safe fonts to maintain design integrity in the PDF output\n- Set appropriate page sizes (A4, Letter, etc.) in the CSS using @page rules for consistent PDF rendering\n\n## Image Guidelines\n- ALWAYS use the Image Tool for image generation or image editing tasks\n- Write a single self-contained image prompt before calling the Image Tool\n- Clearly describe the main subject and overall composition\n- Explicitly specify the intended visual style and aesthetic\n- Provide exact text content if text is required; COMMUNICATION & USER INTERACTION\n\n## 7.1 CONVERSATIONAL INTERACTIONS\nFor casual conversation and social interactions:\n  - ALWAYS use **\'ask\'** tool to end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - NEVER use \'complete\' for casual conversation\n  - Keep responses friendly and natural\n  - Adapt to user\'s communication style\n  - Ask follow-up questions when appropriate (**using \'ask\'**)\n  - Show interest in user\'s responses\n\n## 7.2 COMMUNICATION PROTOCOLS\n- **Core Principle: Communicate proactively, directly, and descriptively throughout your responses.**\n\n- **Narrative-Style Communication:**\n  * Integrate descriptive Markdown-formatted text directly in your responses before, between, and after tool calls\n  * Use a conversational yet efficient tone that conveys what you\'re doing and why\n  * Structure your communication with Markdown headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting for enhanced readability\n  * Balance detail with conciseness - be informative without being verbose\n\n- **Communication Structure:**\n  * Begin tasks with a brief overview of your plan\n  * Provide context headers like `## Planning`, `### Researching`, `## Creating File`, etc.\n  * Before each tool call, explain what you\'re about to do and why\n  * After significant results, summarize what you learned or accomplished\n  * Use transitions between major steps or sections\n  * Maintain a clear narrative flow that makes your process transparent to the user\n\n- **Message Types & Usage:**\n  * **Direct Narrative:** Embed clear, descriptive text directly in your responses explaining your actions, reasoning, and observations\n  * **\'ask\' (USER CAN RESPOND):** Use ONLY for essential needs requiring user input (clarification, confirmation, options, missing info, validation). This blocks execution until user responds.\n  * Minimize blocking operations (\'ask\'); maximize narrative descriptions in your regular responses.\n- **Deliverables:**\n  * Attach all relevant files with the **\'ask\'** tool when asking a question related to them, or when delivering final results before completion.\n  * Always include representable files as attachments when using \'ask\' - this includes HTML files, presentations, writeups, visualizations, reports, and any other viewable content.\n  * For any created files that can be viewed or presented (such as index.html, slides, documents, charts, etc.), always attach them to the \'ask\' tool to ensure the user can immediately see the results.\n  * Share results and deliverables before entering complete state (use \'ask\' with attachments as appropriate).\n  * Ensure users have access to all necessary resources.\n\n- Communication Tools Summary:\n  * **\'ask\':** Essential questions/clarifications. BLOCKS execution. **USER CAN RESPOND.**\n  * **text via markdown format:** Frequent UI/progress updates. NON-BLOCKING. **USER CANNOT RESPOND.**\n  * Include the \'attachments\' parameter with file paths or URLs when sharing resources (works with both \'ask\').\n  * **\'complete\':** Only when ALL tasks are finished and verified. Terminates execution.\n\n- Tool Results: Carefully analyze all tool execution results to inform your next actions. **Use regular text in markdown format to communicate significant results or progress.**\n\n## 7.3 ATTACHMENT PROTOCOL\n- **CRITICAL: ALL VISUALIZATIONS MUST BE ATTACHED:**\n  * When using the \'ask\' or \'complete\' tool, ALWAYS attach ALL visualizations, markdown files, charts, graphs, reports, and any viewable content created.\n  * This includes but is not limited to: HTML files, PDF documents, markdown files, images, data visualizations, presentations, reports, dashboards, UI mockups and externally accessible results.\n  * NEVER mention a visualization or viewable content without attaching it\n  * If you\'ve created multiple visualizations, attach ALL of them\n  * Always make visualizations available to the user BEFORE marking tasks as complete\n  * For web applications or interactive content, always attach the main HTML file\n  * When creating data analysis results, charts must be attached, not just described\n  * Remember: If the user should SEE it, you must ATTACH it with the \'ask\' tool\n  * Verify that ALL visual outputs have been attached before proceeding\n\n- **Attachment Checklist:**\n  * Data visualizations (charts, graphs, plots)\n  * Web interfaces (HTML/CSS/JS files)\n  * Reports and documents (PDF, HTML)\n  * Presentation materials\n  * Images and diagrams\n  * Interactive dashboards\n  * Analysis results with visual components\n  * UI designs and mockups\n  * Any file intended for user viewing or interaction\n\n\n# 8. This module implements a comprehensive Zero Trust security architecture\n//! following NIST SP 800-207 guidelines and IBM\'s Identity-First security paradigm.\n//!\n//! # Components\n//! - Policy components.\n/// Implements the "Never trust, always verify" principle.\npub struct ZeroTrustManager {\n    policy_engine: Arc<RwLock<PolicyEngine>>,\n    trust_engine: Arc<RwLock<TrustEngine>>,\n    authenticator: Arc<RwLock<Authenticator>>,\n    segmentation: Arc<RwLock<SegmentationEngine>>,\n    identity: Arc<RwLock<IdentityFabric>>,\n    enforcement: Arc<RwLock<EnforcementPoint>>,\n    config: duration in seconds\n    pub max_session_duration_secs: u64,\n    /// Enable risk-based authentication\n    pub risk_based_auth_enabled: bool,\n}\n\nimpl Default for ZeroTrustConfig {\n    fn true,\n            identity_fabric_enabled: true,\n            max_session_duration_secs: 28800, // 8 hours\n            risk_based_auth_enabled: true,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Access request std::collections::HashMap<String, serde_json::Value>,\n    /// Identity provider\n    pub identity_provider: Option<String>,\n    /// Device information\n    pub device: Option<DeviceInfo>,\n}\n\n/// Subject types\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub enum SubjectType {\n    User,\n    Service,\n    Device,\n    Application,\n    Workload,\n}\n\n/// Device information\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct DeviceInfo {\n    pub device_id: String,\n    pub device_type: DeviceType,\n    pub os: String,\n    pub Data,\n    Application,\n    Service,\n    API,\n    Infrastructure,\n    Network,\n}\n\n/// Sensitivity levels\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub enum Subscribe,\n}\n\n/// Request context\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct RequestContext {\n    /// Source IP address\n    pub source_ip: String,\n    /// Geolocation\n    pub geo_location: Option<GeoLocation>,\n    /// Time of access\n    pub access_time: chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>,\n    /// Network segment\n    pub network_segment: Option<String>,\n    /// Session ID\n    pub session_id: Option<String>,\n    /// Previous requests in session\n    pub session_request_count: u32,\n    /// Risk indicators\n    pub risk_indicators: String,\n    pub latitude: f64,\n    pub longitude: f64,\n}\n\n/// Risk indicators\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct RiskIndicator {\n    pub indicator_type: RiskIndicatorType,\n    pub severity: f64,\n    pub description: String,\n}\n\n/// Risk indicator types\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub enum RiskIndicatorType {\n    AnomalousLocation,\n    AnomalousTime,\n    AnomalousBehavior,\n    CompromisedCredentials,\n    UnmanagedDevice,\n    VulnerableDevice,\n    ThreatIntelligenceMatch,\n    ImpossibleTravel,\n    BruteForceAttempt,\n    CredentialStuffing,\n}\n\n/// Access decision\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct AccessDecision {\n    /// Decision ID\n    pub id: /// Timestamp\n    pub timestamp: chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>,\n    /// Expiration time (for allow decisions)\n    pub expires_at: Option<chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>>,\n}\n\n/// Decision types\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub enum Decision {\n    Allow,\n    Deny,\n    Challenge,\n    AllowWithObligations,\n}\n\n/// Obligation (conditional requirement)\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct Obligation {\n    pub obligation_type: ObligationType,\n    pub description: String,\n    pub deadline: Option<chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>>,\n}\n\n/// Obligation types\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub enum ObligationType {\n    Reauthenticate,\n    ProvideMFA,\n    ApproveViaManager,\n    CompleteTraining,\n    AcknowledgePolicy,\n    LogAccess,\n    EncryptData,\n    UseVPN,\n}\n\nimpl ZeroTrustManager {\n    /// Create a new Zero Trust Manager\n    pub fn new(config: ZeroTrustConfig) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            policy_engine: Arc::new(RwLock::new(PolicyEngine::new())),\n            trust_engine: Arc::new(RwLock::new(TrustEngine::new())),\n            authenticator: Arc::new(RwLock::new(Authenticator::new())),\n            segmentation: Arc::new(RwLock::new(SegmentationEngine::new())),\n            identity: Arc::new(RwLock::new(IdentityFabric::new())),\n            enforcement: Arc::new(RwLock::new(EnforcementPoint::new())),\n            config,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Evaluate an access request\n    /// \n    /// This is the core Zero Trust evaluation following the principle:\n    /// "Never trust, always verify"\n    pub async fn evaluate_access(&self, request: AccessRequest) -> Result<AccessDecision> {\n        info!("Evaluating access request {} for subject {} to resource {}", \n              request.id, request.subject.id, request.resource.id);\n\n        // Step 1: Verify identity\n        let identity_verified = self.verify_identity(&request).await?;\n        if !identity_verified {\n            return self.deny_access(request.id, "Identity verification failed".to_string()).await;\n        }\n\n        // Step 2: Calculate trust score\n        let trust_score = self.calculate_trust_score(&request).await?;\n        debug!("Trust score for request {}: {}", request.id, trust_score);\n\n        if trust_score < self.config.minimum_trust_score {\n            return self.challenge_access(request.id, trust_score, \n                "Trust score below minimum threshold".to_string()).await;\n        }\n\n        // Step 3: Evaluate policies\n        let policy_decision = self.evaluate_policies(&request).await?;\n        \n        // Step 4: Check segmentation\n        if self.config.segmentation_enabled {\n            let segment_allowed = self.check_segmentation(&request).await?;\n            if !segment_allowed {\n                return self.deny_access(request.id, "Segmentation policy violation".to_string()).await;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Step 5: Generate access decision\n        let decision = self.generate_decision(request, trust_score, policy_decision).await?;\n        \n        // Step 6: Enforce decision\n        self.enforce_decision(&decision).await?;\n\n        Ok(decision)\n    }\n\n    /// Verify identity of the subject\n    async fn verify_identity(&self, request: &AccessRequest) -> Result<bool> {\n        let identity = self.identity.read().await;\n        identity.verify(&request.subject).await\n    }\n\n    /// Calculate trust score for the request\n    async fn calculate_trust_score(&self, request: &AccessRequest) -> Result<f64> {\n        let trust_engine = self.trust_engine.read().await;\n        trust_engine.calculate_score(request).await\n    }\n\n    /// Evaluate policies for the request\n    async fn evaluate_policies(&self, request: &AccessRequest) -> Result<PolicyDecision> {\n        let policy_engine = self.policy_engine.read().await;\n        policy_engine.evaluate(request).await\n    }\n\n    /// Check segmentation policies\n    async fn check_segmentation(&self, request: &AccessRequest) -> Result<bool> {\n        let segmentation = self.segmentation.read().await;\n        segmentation.check_access(&request.subject, &request.resource).await\n    }\n\n    /// Generate final access decision\n    async fn generate_decision(\n        &self, \n        request: AccessRequest, \n        trust_score: f64,\n        policy_decision: PolicyDecision,\n    ) -> Result<AccessDecision> {\n        let decision = match policy_decision.decision {\n            policy::DecisionType::Allow => Decision::Allow,\n            policy::DecisionType::Deny => Decision::Deny,\n            policy::DecisionType::Challenge => Decision::Challenge,\n        };\n\n        Ok(AccessDecision {\n            id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4(),\n            request_id: request.id,\n            decision,\n            trust_score,\n            applied_policies: policy_decision.applied_policies,\n            obligations: policy_decision.obligations.into_iter().map(|o| Obligation {\n                obligation_type: match o {\n                    policy::ObligationType::Reauthenticate => ObligationType::Reauthenticate,\n                    policy::ObligationType::ProvideMFA => ObligationType::ProvideMFA,\n                    policy::ObligationType::ApproveViaManager => ObligationType::ApproveViaManager,\n                    policy::ObligationType::CompleteTraining => ObligationType::CompleteTraining,\n                    policy::ObligationType::AcknowledgePolicy => ObligationType::AcknowledgePolicy,\n                },\n                description: format!("Required: {:?}", o),\n                deadline: None,\n            }).collect(),\n            recommendations: policy_decision.recommendations,\n            timestamp: chrono::Utc::now(),\n            expires_at: Some(chrono::Utc::now() + chrono::Duration::seconds(self.config.max_session_duration_secs as i64)),\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Deny access\n    async fn deny_access(&self, request_id: uuid::Uuid, reason: String) -> Result<AccessDecision> {\n        Ok(AccessDecision {\n            id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4(),\n            request_id,\n            decision: Decision::Deny,\n            trust_score: 0.0,\n            applied_policies: vec![],\n            obligations: vec![],\n            recommendations: vec![reason],\n            timestamp: chrono::Utc::now(),\n            expires_at: None,\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Challenge access (require additional authentication)\n    async fn challenge_access(&self, request_id: uuid::Uuid, trust_score: f64, reason: String) -> Result<AccessDecision> {\n        Ok(AccessDecision {\n            id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4(),\n            request_id,\n            decision: Decision::Challenge,\n            trust_score,\n            applied_policies: vec![],\n            obligations: vec![Obligation {\n                obligation_type: ObligationType::ProvideMFA,\n                description: reason,\n                deadline: Some(chrono::Utc::now() + chrono::Duration::minutes(5)),\n            }],\n            recommendations: vec!["Additional authentication required".to_string()],\n            timestamp: chrono::Utc::now(),\n            expires_at: None,\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Enforce the access decision\n    async fn enforce_decision(&self, decision: &AccessDecision) -> Result<()> {\n        let enforcement = self.enforcement.read().await;\n        enforcement.enforce(decision).await\n    }\n\n    /// Start continuous authentication monitoring\n    pub async fn start_continuous_auth(&self) -> Result<()> {\n        if !self.config.continuous_auth_enabled {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n\n        info!("Starting continuous authentication monitoring");\n        // Continuous auth implementation would run as a background task\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Get current trust statistics\n    pub async fn get_statistics(&self) -> Result<ZeroTrustStatistics> {\n        let trust_engine = self.trust_engine.read().await;\n        let policy_engine = self.policy_engine.read().await;\n        \n        Ok(ZeroTrustStatistics {\n            total_requests: trust_engine.total_requests(),\n            allowed_requests: trust_engine.allowed_requests(),\n            denied_requests: trust_engine.denied_requests(),\n            challenged_requests: trust_engine.challenged_requests(),\n            average_trust_score: trust_engine.average_trust_score(),\n            active_sessions: 0, // Would be tracked by session manager\n            active_policies: policy_engine.policy_count(),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Zero Trust statistics\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]\npub struct ZeroTrustStatistics {\n    pub total_requests: u64,\n    pub allowed_requests: u64,\n    pub denied_requests: u64,\n    pub challenged_requests: u64,\n    pub average_trust_score: f64,\n    pub active_sessions: u64,\n    pub active_policies: usize,\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_zero_trust_manager_creation() {\n        let manager = ZeroTrustManager::new(ZeroTrustConfig::default());\n        assert!(manager.config.minimum_trust_score > 0.0);\n    }\n}\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

Implements the Policy Decision Point (PDP) and Policy Administration Point (PAP)\n//! following XACML and NIST SP 800-207 guidelines.\n\nuse anyhow::{Result, anyhow};\nuse serde::{Serialize, HashMap<String, PolicySet>,\n    default_decision: DecisionType,\n    statistics: PolicyStatistics,\n}\n\n/// Policy Set (collection of policies)\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub created_at: chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>,\n    pub updated_at: chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>,\n}\n\n/// Policy target (what the policy applies to)\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Target {\n    pub subjects: Vec<SubjectMatch>,\n    pub resources: Vec<ResourceMatch>,\n    pub actions: Vec<ActionMatch>,\n    pub environments: Vec<EnvironmentMatch>,\n}\n\n/// Subject matching criteria\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SubjectMatch {\n    pub attribute: String,\n    pub matcher: MatchOperator,\n    pub value: serde_json::Value,\n}\n\n/// Resource matching criteria\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ResourceMatch {\n    pub attribute: String,\n    pub matcher:      let mut weighted_score = 0.0;\n        let mut factors = HashMap::new();\n        \n        // Evaluate each trust factor\n        for factor in &self.factors {\n            let factor_score = self.calculate_risk_adjustment(&request.context.risk_indicators);\n        let final_score = (base_score + risk_adjustment).clamp(0.0, 1.0);\n        \n        debug!("Trust score: base={}, calculate_risk_adjustment(&self, indicators: &[RiskIndicator]) -> f64 {\n        let mut adjustment = 0.0;\n        \n        for indicator in indicators {\n            let penalty = match indicator.indicator_type {\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::AnomalousLocation => -0.15,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::AnomalousTime => -0.10,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::AnomalousBehavior => -0.20,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::CompromisedCredentials => -0.50,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::UnmanagedDevice => -0.25,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::VulnerableDevice => -0.15,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::ThreatIntelligenceMatch => -0.40,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::ImpossibleTravel => -0.35,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::BruteForceAttempt => -0.45,\n                super::RiskIndicatorType::CredentialStuffing => -0.40,\n            };\n            \n            adjustment += penalty * indicator.severity;\n        }\n        \n        adjustment\n    }\n\n    /// Record a trust decision\n    pub fn record_decision(&mut self, score: f64, allowed: bool) {\n        self.statistics.total_requests += 1;\n        self.statistics.total_trust_score += score;\n        \n        if allowed {\n            self.statistics.allowed_requests += 1;\n        } else if score < 0.3 {\n            self.statistics.denied_requests += 1;\n            self.statistics.low_trust_count += 1;\n        } else {\n            self.statistics.challenged_requests += 1;\n        }\n        \n        if score > 0.8 {\n            self.statistics.high_trust_count += 1;\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Get average trust score\n    pub fn average_trust_score(&self) -> f64 {\n        if self.statistics.total_requests == 0 {\n            return 0.5;\n        }\n        self.statistics.total_trust_score / self.statistics.total_requests as f64\n    }\n\n    /// Get total requests\n    pub fn total_requests(&self) -> u64 {\n        self.statistics.total_requests\n    }\n\n    /// Get allowed requests self.statistics.denied_requests\n    }\n\n    /// Get challenged requests count\n    pub fn challenged_requests(&self) -> u64 {\n        self.statistics.challenged_requests\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Default self.weight\n    }\n    \n    async fn evaluate(&self, request: &AccessRequest) -> Result<FactorScore> {\n        let mut score = 0.5; // Base score for unknown device\n        let mut details = super::DeviceType::IoT => score -= 0.1,\n                super::DeviceType::Unknown => score -= 0.15,\n            }\n            \n            // Device risk level\n            score -= calculate_distance(lat1: f64, lon1: f64, lat2: f64, lon2: f64) -> f64 {\n    const EARTH_RADIUS_KM: f64 = 6371.0;\n    \n    let lat1_rad = lat1.to_radians();\n    let lat2_rad = lat2.to_radians();\n    let delta_lat = (lat2 - lat1).to_radians();\n    let delta_lon = (lon2 - lon1).to_radians();\n    \n    let a = (delta_lat / 2.0).sin().powi(2) +\n            lat1_rad.cos() * lat2_rad.cos() * (delta_lon / 2.0).sin().powi(2);\n    let c = 2.0 * a.sqrt().atan2((1.0 - a).sqrt());\n    \n    EARTH_RADIUS_KM * c\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn           return Ok(AuthContext {\n                subject: subject.clone(),\n                method: AuthMethod::Password, // Default\n                timestamp: Utc::now(),\n                result:         best_result = result;\n                best_strength = strength;\n                best_method = method.method_type();\n            }\n            \n            if result == AuthResult::Success     }\n        } else {\n            best_result\n        };\n        \n        // Create session on successful auth\n        let session_id = if final_result == AuthResult::Success {\n            Some(self.create_session(subject, best_method.clone(), best_strength).await?)\n        } else {\n            None\n        };\n        \n        Ok(AuthContext {\n            subject: risk_score: 0.0, // Would be calculated\n            claims: HashMap::new(),\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Verify identity (for Zero Trust)\n    pub async fn verify(&self, subject: &Subject) -> SessionStatus::Active && s.expires_at > Utc::now()\n        });\n        \n        Ok(has_active_session)\n    }\n\n    /// Create a new session\n    async fn create_session(\n        &mut self,\n    challenge_type,\n            created_at: Utc::now(),\n            expires_at: Utc::now() + Duration::minutes(5),\n            attempts: 0,\n            status: ChallengeStatus::Pending,\n      // Check if identity exists and is active\n        let identity = match self.identities.get(&subject.id) {\n            Some(id) => id,\n            None => {\n                debug!("Identity {} not found", subject.id);\n                return Ok(false);\n            }\n        };\n        \n        if identity.status != IdentityStatus::Active {\n            warn!("Identity {} is not active:         warn!("Identity {} assurance level {:?} below minimum {:?}",\n                  subject.id, identity.assurance_level, self.config.min_assurance_level);\n            return Ok(false);\n SessionStatus::Active && s.expires_at > Utc::now());\n        \n        if !has_active_session {\n            debug!("No active session for identity {}", subject.id);\n            // Still allow if   // Try to find existing identity\n        if let Some(existing) = self.identities.get(&provider_identity.id) {\n            return Ok(existing.clone());\n        }\n        \n        // Create new      };\n        \n        self.identities.insert(identity.id.clone(), identity.clone());\n        Ok(identity)\n    }\n\n    /// Validate session\n    pub fn validate_session(&mut self, session_id: SessionStatus::Active {\n            return Ok(false);\n        }\n        \n        if session.expires_at < Utc::now() {\n            session.status = SessionStatus::Expired;\n            return    }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Link identities\n    pub fn link_identities(&mut self, identity1: &str, identity2: &str) -> Result<()> {\n        if !self.identities.contains_key(identity1) {\n            return Err(anyhow!("Identity {} not found", identity1));\n        }\n        if !self.identities.contains_key(identity2) {\n            return Err(anyhow!("Identity {} not found", identity2));\n        }\n        \n        self.identity_links\n            .entry(identity1.to_string())\n            .or_insert_with(Vec::new)\n            .push(identity2.to_string());\n        \n        self.identity_links\n            .entry(identity2.to_string())\n            .or_insert_with(Vec::new)\n            .push(identity1.to_string());\n        \n        info!("Linked identities {} and {}", identity1, identity2);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Get linked identities\n    pub fn get_linked_identities(&self, identity_id: &str) -> Vec<&Identity> {\n        self.identity_links\n            .get(identity_id)\n            .map(|ids| {\n                ids.iter()\n                    .filter_map(|id| self.identities.get(id))\n                    .collect()\n            })\n            .unwrap_or_default()\n    }\n\n    /// Sync identities from all providers\n    pub async fn sync_all(&mut self) -> Result<usize> {\n        if !self.config.sync_enabled {\n            return Ok(0);\n        }\n        \n        let mut total_synced = 0;\n        \n        for (provider_id, provider) in &self.providers {\n            match provider.sync().await {\n                Ok(identities) => {\n                    for pi in identities {\n                        if let Ok(identity) = self.get_or_create_identity(&pi, provider_id).await {\n                            total_synced += 1;\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n                Err(e) => {\n                    warn!("Failed to sync from provider {}: {}", provider_id, e);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        info!("Synced {} identities from all providers", total_synced);\n        Ok(total_synced)\n    }\n\n    /// Get identity count\n    pub fn identity_count(&self) -> usize {\n        self.identities.len()\n    }\n\n    /// Get active session count\n    pub fn active_session_count(&self) -> usize {\n        self.sessions.values()\n            .filter(|s| s.status == SessionStatus::Active && s.expires_at > Utc::now())\n            .count()\n    }\n\n    /// List all identities\n    pub fn list_identities(&self) -> Vec<&Identity> }\n}\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

  pub pending_obligations: Vec<Obligation>,\n    /// Fulfilled obligations\n    pub fulfilled_obligations: Vec<Obligation>,\n    /// Created at\n    pub created_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    /// Expires serde_json::Value>,\n    pub result: EnforcementResult,\n}\n\n/// Enforcement actions\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum EnforcementAction {\n    DecisionEnforced,\n    DecisionRevoked,\n    ObligationCreated,\n    ObligationFulfilled,\n    ObligationFailed,\n    AccessGranted,\n    AccessDenied,\n    ChallengeIssued,\n    SessionCreated,\n    SessionTerminated,\n}\n\n/// Enforcement result\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum EnforcementResult {\n    Success,\n    Failure,\n    Partial,\n}\n\n/// Enforcement {\n        Self {\n            active_decisions: HashMap::new(),\n            obligation_handlers: HashMap::new(),\n            audit_log: Vec::new(),\n            statistics: EnforcementStatistics::default(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Register an obligation handler\n    pub fn register_handler(&mut self, handler: Box<dyn ObligationHandler + Send + Sync>) {\n        let access decision\n    pub async fn enforce(&self, decision: &AccessDecision) -> Result<()> {\n        info!("Enforcing decision {} for request {}", decision.decision_id, decision.request_id);\n        \n        match decision.decision {\n            Decision::Allow => {\n                self.enforce_allow(decision).await?;\n            }\n            Decision::Deny => {\n                self.enforce_deny(decision).await?;\n            }\n            Decision::Challenge => {\n                self.enforce_challenge(decision).await?;\n            }\n            Decision::AllowWithObligations => {\n                self.enforce_with_obligations(decision).await?;\n            }\n        }\n        \n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Enforce allow decision\n    async fn enforce_allow(&self, decision: &AccessDecision) -> Result<()> {\n        info!("Access ALLOWED for request {}", decision.request_id);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Enforce deny decision\n    async fn enforce_deny(&self, decision: &AccessDecision) -> Result<()> {\n        info!("Access DENIED for request {}", decision.request_id);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Enforce challenge decision\n    async fn enforce_challenge(&self, decision: &AccessDecision) -> Result<()> {\n        info!("Access CHALLENGE required for request {}", decision.request_id);\n        \n        // Issue challenges for obligations\n        for obligation in &decision.obligations {\n            debug!("Issuing obligation: {:?}", obligation.obligation_type);\n        }\n        \n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Enforce decision with obligations\n    async fn enforce_with_obligations(&self, decision: &AccessDecision) -> Result<()> {\n        info!("Access ALLOWED WITH OBLIGATIONS for request {}", decision.request_id);\n        \n        // Record obligations to be fulfilled\n        for obligation in &decision.obligations {\n            debug!("Obligation required: {:?}", obligation.obligation_type);\n        }\n        \n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Record a decision (stores it for tracking)\n    pub fn record_decision(&mut self, decision: &AccessDecision, subject_id: &str, resource_id: &str) -> Result<String> {\n        let active = ActiveDecision {\n            decision_id: decision.decision_id.to_string(),\n            request_id: decision.request_id.to_string(),\n            subject_id: subject_id.to_string(),\n            resource_id: resource_id.to_string(),\n            decision: decision.decision,\n            trust_score: decision.trust_score,\n            pending_obligations: decision.obligations.clone(),\n            fulfilled_obligations: vec![],\n            created_at: decision.timestamp,\n            expires_at: decision.expires_at,\n            status: if decision.obligations.is_empty() {\n                DecisionStatus::Active\n            } else {\n                DecisionStatus::ObligationPending\n            },\n        };\n        \n        self.active_decisions.insert(active.decision_id.clone(), active.clone());\n        \n        // Update statistics\n        self.statistics.total_decisions += 1;\n        match decision.decision {\n            Decision::Allow => self.statistics.allow_count += 1,\n            Decision::Deny => self.statistics.deny_count += 1,\n            Decision::Challenge => self.statistics.challenge_count += 1,\n            Decision::AllowWithObligations => self.statistics.allow_count += 1,\n        }\n        \n        // Create audit entry\n        self.add_audit_entry(active.decision_id.clone(), EnforcementAction::DecisionEnforced, decision);\n        \n        Ok(active.decision_id)\n    }\n\n    /// Check if obligation is fulfilled\n    pub async fn check_obligation(&mut self, decision_id: &str, obligation_idx: usize) -> Result<bool> {\n        let decision = self.active_decisions.get_mut(decision_id)\n            .ok_or_else(|| anyhow!("Decision {} not found", decision_id))?;\n        \n        if obligation_idx >= decision.pending_obligations.len() {\n            return Err(anyhow!("Invalid obligation index"));\n        }\n        \n        let obligation = decision.pending_obligations[obligation_idx].clone();\n        let handler_key = format!("{:?}", obligation.obligation_type);\n        \n        if let Some(handler) = self.obligation_handlers.get(&handler_key) {\n            let context = EnforcementContext {\n                subject_id: decision.subject_id.clone(),\n                resource_id: decision.resource_id.clone(),\n                session_id: None,\n                additional: HashMap::new(),\n            };\n            \n            let fulfilled = handler.fulfill(&obligation, &context).await?;\n            \n            if fulfilled {\n                // Move obligation to fulfilled\n                let obligation = decision.pending_obligations.remove(obligation_idx);\n                decision.fulfilled_obligations.push(obligation);\n                \n                // Update status if all obligations fulfilled\n                if decision.pending_obligations.is_empty() {\n                    decision.status = DecisionStatus::Active;\n                }\n                \n                self.statistics.obligations_fulfilled += 1;\n                self.add_audit_entry(decision_id.to_string(), EnforcementAction::ObligationFulfilled, &obligation);\n                \n                return Ok(true);\n            }\n        }\n        \n        self.statistics.obligations_failed += 1;\n        Ok(false)\n    }\n\n    /// Revoke a decision\n    pub fn revoke_decision(&mut self, decision_id: &str, reason: &str) -> Result<()> {\n        let decision = self.active_decisions.get_mut(decision_id)\n            .ok_or_else(|| anyhow!("Decision {} not found", decision_id))?;\n        \n        decision.status = DecisionStatus::Revoked;\n        self.statistics.revocations += 1;\n        \n        self.add_audit_entry(\n            decision_id.to_string(), \n            EnforcementAction::DecisionRevoked,\n            &format!("Revoked: {}", reason)\n        );\n        \n        info!("Revoked decision {}: {}", decision_id, reason);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Check if decision is still valid\n    pub fn is_decision_valid(&self, decision_id: &str) -> bool {\n        if let Some(decision) = self.active_decisions.get(decision_id) {\n            if decision.status != DecisionStatus::Active && decision.status != DecisionStatus::ObligationPending {\n                return false;\n            }\n            \n            if let Some(expires) = decision.expires_at {\n                if expires < Utc::now() {\n                    return false;\n                }\n            }\n            \n            return true;\n        }\n        false\n    }\n\n    /// Get active decision\n    pub fn get_decision(&self, decision_id: &str) -> Option<&ActiveDecision> {\n        self.active_decisions.get(decision_id)\n    }\n\n    /// Get all active decisions for a subject\n    pub fn get_subject_decisions(&self, subject_id: &str) -> Vec<&ActiveDecision> {\n        self.active_decisions.values()\n            .filter(|d| d.subject_id == subject_id && d.status == DecisionStatus::Active)\n            .collect()\n    }\n\n    /// Get all active decisions for a resource\n    pub fn get_resource_decisions(&self, resource_id: &str) -> Vec<&ActiveDecision> {\n        self.active_decisions.values()\n            .filter(|d| d.resource_id == resource_id && d.status == DecisionStatus::Active)\n            .collect()\n    }\n\n    /// Clean up expired decisions\n    pub fn cleanup_expired(&mut self) -> usize {\n        let now = Utc::now();\n        let expired: Vec<String> = self.active_decisions.iter()\n            .filter(|(_, d)| {\n                d.expires_at.map(|e| e < now).unwrap_or(false) || d.status == DecisionStatus::Expired\n            })\n            .map(|(id, _)| id.clone())\n            .collect();\n        \n        for id in &expired {\n            if let Some(decision) = self.active_decisions.get_mut(id) {\n                decision.status = DecisionStatus::Expired;\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if !expired.is_empty() {\n            info!("Cleaned up {} expired decisions", expired.len());\n        }\n        \n        expired.len()\n    }\n\n    /// Add audit entry\n    fn add_audit_entry<T: Serialize>(&mut self, decision_id: String, action: EnforcementAction, details: &T) {\n        let entry = EnforcementAuditEntry {\n            id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4().to_string(),\n            decision_id,\n            action,\n            timestamp: Utc::now(),\n            details: serde_json::to_value(details)\n                .and_then(|v| serde_json::from_value(v))\n                .unwrap_or_default(),\n            result: EnforcementResult::Success,\n        };\n        \n        self.audit_log.push(entry);\n    }\n\n    /// Get statistics\n    pub fn get_statistics(&self) -> &EnforcementStatistics {\n        &self.statistics\n    }\n\n    /// Get audit log\n    pub fn get_audit_log(&self, limit: usize) -> Vec<&EnforcementAuditEntry> {\n        self.audit_log.iter().rev().take(limit).collect()\n    }\n\n    /// Get active decision count\n    pub fn active_decision_count(&self) -> usize {\n        self.active_decisions.values()\n            .filter(|d| d.status == DecisionStatus::Active)\n            .count()\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Default for EnforcementPoint {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self::new()\n    }\n}\n\n// Default }\n}\n\n#[async_trait::async_trait]\nimpl ObligationHandler for MFAObligationHandler {\n    fn obligation_type(&self) -> ObligationType {\n        ObligationType::ProvideMFA\n    }\n    \n    async fn is_fulfilled(&self, _obligation: &Obligation) -> bool {\n        false\n    }\n}\n\n/// Reauthentication Obligation Handler\npub struct ReauthObligationHandler;\n\nimpl ReauthObligationHandler {\n discovery scan\n    pub async fn run_discovery(&self) -> Result<Vec<DiscoveredAI>> {\n        info!("Starting Shadow AI discovery scan");\n        \n        let mut discovery = self.discovery.write().await;\n        let discovered = discovery.scan_all().await?;\n        \n        info!("Discovery complete: found {} AI instances", discovered.len());\n        Ok(discovered)\n    }\n\n    /// Analyze traffic for AI patterns\n    pub async fn analyze_traffic(&self, traffic_data: &[u8]) -> Result<Vec<AITrafficPattern>> {\n        if !self.config.traffic_analysis_enabled {\n            return Ok(vec![]);\n        }\n        \n        let analyzer = self.traffic_analyzer.read().await;\n        analyzer.analyze(traffic_data).await\n    }\n\n    /// Assess risk of discovered AI\n    pub async fn assess_risk(&self, discovered: &DiscoveredAI) -> Result<(f64, RiskLevel)> {\n        let risk = self.risk_assessment.read().await;\n        risk.calculate(discovered).await\n    }\n\n    /// Check governance status\n    pub async fn check_governance(&self, model_id: &str) -> Result<GovernanceStatus> {\n        let governance = self.governance.read().await;\n        governance.get_status(model_id).await\n    }\n\n    /// Process discovered AI (assess risk, check governance, recommend actions)\n    pub async fn process_discovery(&self, discovered: DiscoveredAI) -> Result<DetectionResult> {\n        // Assess risk\n        let (risk_score, risk_level) = self.assess_risk(&discovered).await?;\n        \n        // Check governance status\n        let governance_status = self.check_governance(&discovered.id).await?;\n        \n        // Generate recommended actions\n        let recommended_actions = self.generate_recommendations(risk_score, governance_status).await?;\n        \n        Ok(DetectionResult {\n            id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4().to_string(),\n            discovered,\n            risk_score,\n            risk_level,\n  async fn generate_recommendations(\n        &self,\n        risk_score: f64,\n        governance_status: GovernanceStatus,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<GovernanceAction>> {\n        let mut actions = Vec::new();\n        \n        if risk_score >= self.config.alert_risk_threshold {\n            actions.push(GovernanceAction::Alert);\n        }\n        \n        if governance_status == GovernanceStatus::Unapproved {\n            actions.push(GovernanceAction::RequestApproval);\n        }\n        \n        if risk_score >= 0.9 && self.config.auto_block_high_risk {\n            actions.push(GovernanceAction::Block);\n        }\n        \n        if governance_status == GovernanceStatus::Pending {\n            actions.push(GovernanceAction::ExpediteReview);\n        }\n        \n        Ok(actions)\n    }\n\n    /// Register an AI model for governance\n    pub async fn register_model(&self, model: AIModel) -> Result<()> {\n        let mut governance = self.governance.write().await;\n        governance.register(model).await\n    }\n\n    /// Approve an AI model\n    pub async fn approve_model(&self, model_id: &str, approver: &str, justification: /// Record usage event\n    pub async fn record_usage(&self, event: AIUsageEvent) -> Result<()> {\n        // Analyze the usage event for risk indicators\n        let risk = self.risk_assessment.read().await;\n        let _risk_score = risk.analyze_usage(&event).await?;\n        \n        // Could trigger alerts based on usage patterns\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    ///   sample.to_string()\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Analyze HTTP request\n    pub async fn analyze_http(&self, request: &HTTPRequest) -> Result<Vec<AITrafficPattern>> {\n        let mut patterns = Vec::new();\n        \n        // Check headers\n        for (key, value) in &request.headers {\n            let header_data = format!("{}: {}", key, value);\n            let header_patterns = self.analyze(header_data.as_bytes()).await?;\n            patterns.extend(header_patterns);\n        }\n        \n        // Check body\n        if let Some(ref body) = request.body {\n            let body_patterns = self.analyze(body.as_bytes()).await?;\n            patterns.extend(body_patterns);\n        }\n        \n        // Check URL\n        let url_patterns = self.analyze(request.url.as_bytes()).await?;\n        patterns.extend(url_patterns);\n        \n        Ok(patterns)\n    }\n\n    /// Add custom signature\n    pub fn add_signature(&mut self, add_default_factors(&mut self) {\n        let factors = vec![\n            RiskFactor {\n                id: "data-exposure".to_string(),\n                name: "Data Exposure Risk".to_string(),\n                description: "Risk of sensitive data being exposed to AI".to_string(),\n                weight: 0.25,\n                factor_type: RiskFactorType::DataExposure,\n                scoring: RiskScoring {\n                    scoring_type: ScoringType::Step,\n                    thresholds: vec![\n                        (0.0, 0.1),   // No sensitive data\n                        (0.3, 0.3),   // Internal data\n                        (0.5, 0.5),   // Confidential data\n                        (0.7, 0.8),   // Restricted data\n                        (0.9, 1.0),   // Top secret data\n                    ],\n                },\n            },\n            RiskFactor {\n                id: "provider-trust".to_string(),\n                name: "Provider Trust Level".to_string(),\n                description: "Trust level of the AI provider".to_string(),\n                weight: 0.20,\n                factor_type: RiskFactorType::ProviderTrust,\n                scoring: RiskScoring {\n                    scoring_type: ScoringType::Step,\n                    thresholds: vec![\n                        (1.0, 0.1),   // Internal\n                        (0.9, 0.2),   // Enterprise agreement\n                        (0.7, 0.4),   // Known provider\n                        (0.5, 0.6),   // Unknown provider\n                        (0.0, 0.9),   // Untrusted\n                    ],\n                },\n            },\n            RiskFactor {\n                id: "unauthorized-access".to_string(),\n                name: "Unauthorized Access Risk".to_string(),\n                description: "Risk of unauthorized users accessing AI".to_string(),\n                weight: 0.15,\n                factor_type: RiskFactorType::UnauthorizedAccess,\n                scoring: RiskScoring {\n                    scoring_type: ScoringType::Linear,\n                    thresholds: vec![],\n                },\n            },\n            RiskFactor {\n                id: "compliance-violation".to_string(),\n                name: "Compliance Violation Risk".to_string(),\n                description: "Risk of violating compliance requirements".to_string(),\n                weight: 0.20,\n                factor_type: RiskFactorType::ComplianceViolation,\n                scoring: RiskScoring {\n                    scoring_type: ScoringType::Step,\n                    thresholds: vec![\n                        (0.0, 0.1),\n                        (0.5, 0.5),\n                        (1.0, 0.9),\n                    ],\n                },\n            },\n            RiskFactor {\n                id: "data-leakage".to_string(),\n                name: "Data Leakage Risk".to_string(),\n                description: "Risk of data being leaked through AI responses".to_string(),\n                weight: 0.20,\n                factor_type: RiskFactorType::DataLeakage,\n                scoring: RiskScoring {\n                    scoring_type: ScoringType::Linear,\n                    thresholds: vec![],\n                },\n            },\n        ];\n        \n        self.factors = factors;\n    }\n\n    /// Calculate risk for a discovered AI\n    pub async fn calculate(&self, discovered: &DiscoveredAI) -> Result<(f64, RiskLevel)> {\n        info!("Calculating risk for AI: {}", discovered.id);\n        \n        let mut total_score = 0.0;\n        let mut total_weight = 0.0;\n        \n        // Calculate data exposure risk\n        let data_risk = self.calculate_data_risk(discovered);\n        total_score += data_risk * self.get_factor_weight("data-exposure");\n        total_weight += self.get_factor_weight("data-exposure");\n        \n        // Calculate provider trust risk\n        let provider_risk = self.calculate_provider_risk(discovered);\n        total_score += provider_risk * self.get_factor_weight("provider-trust");\n        total_weight += self.get_factor_weight("provider-trust");\n        \n        // Factor in risk indicators\n        let indicator_penalty = discovered.risk_indicators.len() as f64 * 0.05;\n        total_score += indicator_penalty;\n        \n        // Normalize score\n        let final_score = if total_weight > 0.0 {\n            (total_score / total_weight).min(1.0)\n        } else {\n            0.5\n        };\n        \n        let risk_level = self.score_to_level(final_score);\n        \n        debug!("Risk score for {}: {} ({:?})", discovered.id, final_score, risk_level);\n        \n        Ok((final_score, risk_level))\n    }\n\n    /// Calculate data risk\n    fn calculate_data_risk(&self, discovered: &DiscoveredAI) -> f64 {\n        let data_types = &discovered.details.data_types;\n        \n        // Check for sensitive data types\n        let sensitive_types = ["pii", "phi", "financial", "credentials", "secrets"];\n        let has_sensitive = data_types.iter()\n            .any(|dt| sensitive_types.iter().any(|st| dt.to_lowercase().contains(st)));\n        \n        if has_sensitive {\n            0.8\n        } else if !data_types.is_empty() {\n            0.4\n        } else {\n            0.2\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Calculate provider risk\n    fn calculate_provider_risk(&self, discovered: &DiscoveredAI) -> f64 {\n        if let Some(ref provider) = discovered.details.provider {\n            match provider.to_lowercase().as_str() {\n                "internal" | "self-hosted" => 0.1,\n                "openai" | "anthropic" => 0.3,\n                "azure" | "aws" | "gcp" => 0.35,\n                _ => 0.6,\n            }\n        } else {\n            0.7 // Unknown provider\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Get factor weight\n    fn get_factor_weight(&self, factor_id: &str) -> f64 {\n        self.factors.iter()\n            .find(|f| f.id == factor_id)\n            .map(|f| f.weight)\n            .unwrap_or(0.0)\n    }\n\n    /// Convert score to risk level\n    fn score_to_level(&self, score: f64) -> RiskLevel {\n        if score >= self.thresholds.critical {\n            RiskLevel::Critical\n        } else if score >= self.thresholds.high {\n            RiskLevel::High\n        } else if score >= self.thresholds.medium {\n            RiskLevel::Medium\n        } else if score >= self.thresholds.low {\n            RiskLevel::Low\n        } else {\n            RiskLevel::Minimal\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Analyze usage event for risk\n    pub async fn analyze_usage(&self, event: &AIUsageEvent) -> Result<f64> {\n        let mut risk_score = 0.0;\n        \n        // Check data classification\n        let classification_risk = match event.data_classification {\n            DataClassification::Public => 0.1,\n            DataClassification::Internal => 0.2,\n            DataClassification::Confidential => 0.5,\n            DataClassification::Restricted => 0.8,\n            DataClassification::Sensitive => 0.9,\n        };\n        risk_score += classification_risk * 0.4;\n        \n        // Check risk indicators\n        let indicator_risk = event.risk_indicators.len() as f64 * 0.1;\n        risk_score += indicator_risk * 0.3;\n        \n        // Check request size (large requests may indicate data exfiltration)\n        let size_risk = if event.request_size > 100_000 {\n            0.3\n        } else if event.request_size > 10_000 {\n            0.1\n        } else {\n            0.0\n        };\n        risk_score += size_risk * 0.3;\n        \n        Ok(risk_score.min(1.0))\n    }\n\n    /// Get detailed risk assessment\n    pub async fn get_detailed_assessment(&self, discovered: &DiscoveredAI) -> Result<RiskScore> {\n        let (overall_score, risk_level) = self.calculate(discovered).await?;\n        \n        // Calculate individual factor scores\n        let mut factor_scores = HashMap::new();\n        factor_scores.insert("data_exposure".to_string(), self.calculate_data_risk(discovered));\n        factor_scores.insert("provider_trust".to_string(), self.calculate_provider_risk(discovered));\n        \n        // Generate risk indicators\n        let mut risk_indicators = Vec::new();\n        \n        if !discovered.risk_indicators.is_empty() {\n            risk_indicators.push(RiskIndicator {\n                indicator_type: "detected_indicators".to_string(),\n                severity: 0.7,\n                description: format!("Detected risk indicators: {}", discovered.risk_indicators.join(", ")),\n                remediation: Some("Review and address detected risk indicators".to_string()),\n            });\n        }\n        \n        if discovered.details.api_key_masked.is_some() {\n            risk_indicators.push(RiskIndicator {\n                indicator_type: "api_key_exposed".to_string(),\n                severity: 0.8,\n                description: "API key detected in configuration".to_string(),\n                remediation: Some("Rotate API key and store securely".to_string()),\n            });\n        }\n        \n        // Generate recommendations\n        let mut recommendations = Vec::new();\n        \n        if risk_level >= RiskLevel::High {\n            recommendations.push("Consider blocking this AI until approved".to_string());\n        }\n        if risk_level >= RiskLevel::Medium {\n            recommendations.push("Request formal approval for this AI".to_string());\n        }\n        if !discovered.details.users.is_empty() {\n            recommendations.push("Review user access to this AI".to_string());\n        }\n        \n        Ok(RiskScore {\n            id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4().to_string(),\n            model_id: discovered.id.clone(),\n            overall_score,\n            risk_level,\n            factor_scores,\n            risk_indicators,\n            recommendations,\n            timestamp: Utc::now(),\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Add custom risk factor\n    pub fn add_factor(&mut self, factor: RiskFactor) -> Result<()> {\n        info!("Adding risk factor: {}", factor.name);\n        self.factors.push(factor);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Get risk factors\n    pub fn get_factors(&self) -> &[RiskFactor] {\n        &self.factors\n    }\n\n    /// Record risk score in history\n    pub fn record_score(&mut self, score: &RiskScore) {\n        self.risk_history\n            .entry(score.model_id.clone())\n            .or_insert_with(Vec::new)\n            .push(score.clone());\n    }\n\n    /// Get risk history for a model\n    pub fn get_risk_history(&self, model_id: &str) -> Option<&[RiskScore]> {\n        self.risk_history.get(model_id).map(|v| v.as_slice())\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Default for RiskAssessment {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self::new()\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use test_risk_level_conversion() {\n        let assessment = RiskAssessment::new();\n        \n        assert_eq!(assessment.score_to_level(0.1), RiskLevel::Minimal);\n        assert_eq!(assessment.score_to_level(0.3), RiskLevel::Low);\n        assert_eq!(assessment.score_to_level(0.5), RiskLevel::Medium);\n        assert_eq!(assessment.score_to_level(0.7),
